12 Domains62 Workflows
Client Experience Playbook Agent
C-Suite & ABM
FMs/DSs manually search 5+ systems (Adobe, Seismic, Lighthouse, W3 Box) for assets. 6-8 hrs per playbook. ~160 requestors can't be served manually. Named Accounts: ~300-500 -> 2,20
#1
Brief Description

Dynamically assembles personalized, CXO-ready client experience playbooks by aggregating relevant assets, events, and best practices from across IBM systems, aligned to specific account segments, industries, and roles, to enable ABM execution at scale for 2,200+ named accounts.

Process Owners
  • Eric Niu
  • Elena Louros
  • Cheryl Caudill
  • Jen Knecht
  • Steve Collins
  • Mark Overstreet
  • CIO
User Groups
  • FMs/DSs: Requestors
  • Playbook team: Operators
  • Sales: Consumers
  • MCC domains: Contributors
Future State: What AI Does
AI-Enabled Workflow
  • SEARCH: Query 5+ systems in parallel with unified taxonomy.
  • RANK: By relevance, currency; de-duplicate.
  • ASSEMBLE: Populate template with top assets/journeys.
  • CONVERSE: Iterative refinement.
  • REFRESH: Surface new content for new time windows.
Business Impact High

ABM personalization across 2,200 accounts. 6-8 hrs -> minutes. C-suite relationship broadening. Competitive imperative. 'Trigger point for all downstream activities.'

Time Savings
  • ~160 FMs/DSs. Potentially 703+484 FTEs if self-serve. Sales/consulting downstream.
Future Extensions & Reusability
  • HIGH: Domain-agnostic content curation. Self-serve for sellers. Unified taxonomy for all MCC.
  • MVP: Elena's team + CIO. Scale: ~160 FM/DS -> sales/consulting.
Feasibility High
  • Source systems known; process validated. Risks: taxonomy inconsistency; People.ai not at scale; no CIO engagement.
  • [RISK: no CIO engagement initiated]
  • [RISK: People.ai not at scale — timeline unknown]
Primary Friction Points
  • 1. Manual aggregation across 5+ systems
  • 2. No unified taxonomy
  • 3. Outdated content surfaces alongside current
  • 4. No unified MCC asset view
  • 5. Cross-domain coordination manual
  • 6. Inconsistency at scale
Technical Requirements
Data Sources
  • Workfront, Adobe, Seismic, Lighthouse, W3 Box, ISC, TAP 360, People.ai
  • [OPEN: API capabilities for Seismic, Lighthouse, W3 Box?]
System / Integration Requirements
  • Multi-system search agent. Unified taxonomy layer. Conversational front-end. Template engine. Currency filter.
Candidate Vendors / Tools
  • Watsonx.ai/orchestrate, MCC Advisor, Romy's automations, Consulting AI packs, Buyer Insights
Other Dependencies & Open Items
  • CRITICAL: Content tagging; CIO engagement.
  • HIGH: MCC Advisor alignment; ISC quality.
  • MEDIUM: People.ai; prioritization competition.
  • 1. Content governance ownership
  • 2. Delivery mechanism
  • 3. People.ai timeline
  • 4. Team FTE count
  • 5. Revenue metrics
  • 6. API capabilities
KPI's
  • Time to assemble client playbook (current: 4-6 hrs; target: <30 min)
  • Playbook accuracy / relevance score rated by field sellers (target: >85%)
  • % of client engagements using AI-generated playbooks vs. manual prep
Growth Impact
Domain-agnostic content curation
Productivity Impact
6-8 hrs -> minutes
Discovery Gaps 16 gaps
All identified gaps for this workflow requiring follow-up investigation or resolution

14 How many FTEs are on the team's playbook team? What is their current capacity in playbooks per week? Inline [GAP]
15 Can we quantify the revenue impact of personalized ABM plays vs. generic engagement? Any conversion or pipeline metrics? Inline [GAP]
16 What are the API capabilities of Seismic, Lighthouse, and W3 Box? Are there existing connectors or must they be built? Inline [GAP]
IBM Consulting / © 2026 IBM Corporation | MCC & IBM Confidential Client Experience Playbook Agent  |  Workflow Blueprint
Executive Engagement Briefing Agent
C-Suite & ABM
600+ packets/yr, 100% positive feedback. External analysts conduct research. AI can't scrape LinkedIn, fails at formatting. 4-8 hrs per packet. 3 versions. Secure Box distribution.
#2
Brief Description

Automates the research, assembly, and formatting of comprehensive executive briefing packets for IBM senior leaders preparing for CXO client engagements, roundtables, and industry events.

Process Owners
  • Elena Louros
  • Eric Niu
  • Cheryl Caudill
  • ELT/VP+
  • SLE/CXO Programs
  • MLE
  • Privacy office
User Groups
  • Elena's team: Research
  • SLE/CXO: Events
  • Executive offices: Review
  • Field marketers: Consumers
Future State: What AI Does
AI-Enabled Workflow
  • INTAKE: Workfront request.
  • RESEARCH: Auto-pull internal + PIA-compliant external.
  • RESOLVE: Internal/external discrepancies.
  • FORMAT: Populate templates.
  • DISTRIBUTE: Secure Box.
  • FEEDBACK: Debrief capture.
Business Impact High

600+ packets, 100% positive. Executives 'never more prepared.' Cost savings. Vision: full-scale account insights engine.

Time Savings
  • Elena + analysts. All ELT/VP+. Event managers. Field marketers (restricted).
Future Extensions & Reusability
  • VERY HIGH: Account intelligence engine. Seller onboarding. MLE synergy. Buying group navigation.
  • Vision: any executive engagement. MLE synergy. CIO, CDO, Privacy needed.
Feasibility Medium
  • Internal data accessible. Risks: LinkedIn; PIA; AI formatting. Existing agents offer reuse.
  • [RISK: LinkedIn scraping blocked by PIA]
  • [OPEN: PIA status for external data?]
Primary Friction Points
  • 1. 4-8 hrs manual per packet
  • 2. AI can't scrape LinkedIn
  • 3. AI fails multi-column formatting
  • 4. ISC outdated
  • 5. PIA restricts distribution
  • 6. No post-engagement feedback
  • 7. Multiple template variants
Technical Requirements
Data Sources
  • Workfront, W3 Box, AI Prompt Library, ISC, Client Business Value, LinkedIn (manual), Event Registration
System / Integration Requirements
  • Internal aggregation. External research (PIA-compliant). Conflict resolution. Template engine. Secure distribution. Feedback loop.
Candidate Vendors / Tools
  • Consulting AI Packs, Buyer Insights, Romy's automations, External vendor TBD
Other Dependencies & Open Items
  • CRITICAL: PIA; LinkedIn; CIO.
  • HIGH: ISC quality; AI formatting; MLE coordination.
  • MEDIUM: Analyst dependency; feedback gap.
  • 1. Post-engagement process
  • 2. Analyst team size/cost
  • 3. Pipeline impact metrics
  • 4. PIA status
  • 5. MLE overlap
KPI's
  • Briefing packet preparation time (current: 6-8 hrs; target: <1 hr)
  • % of C-suite meetings with AI-generated briefing packets (target: 100%)
  • Executive satisfaction score on briefing quality (target: >4/5)
  • [OPEN: pipeline impact metrics not yet defined]
Growth Impact
Account intelligence engine
Productivity Impact
Creation: minutes vs

IBM Consulting / © 2026 IBM Corporation | MCC & IBM Confidential Executive Engagement Briefing Agent  |  Workflow Blueprint
C-Suite Contact Accuracy & Account Targeting Agent
C-Suite & ABM
ISC CXO records 'very often inaccurate.' Manual system of record attempted for ~400-500 accounts; not updated since 2,200 expansion. Copilot ~30-40% accuracy. ZoomInfo 'behind the
#3
Brief Description

Continuously validates C-suite contact data across IBM systems using external corroboration, then enables precision targeting of CXO contacts by correlating accurate contact records with engagement history, opportunity data, and marketing insights.

Process Owners
  • Eric Niu
  • Elena Louros
  • CDO (Paul Ambraz)
  • Thomas Reinecke
  • Sellers
User Groups
  • CXO team: Lookups
  • CDO: Governance
  • Rev Tech: Integration
  • Sellers: Validation
Future State: What AI Does
AI-Enabled Workflow
  • STAGE 1: Ingest ISC -> corroborate external -> notify sellers -> update via CDO pipeline.
  • STAGE 2: Correlate with TAP 360/ISC pipeline -> output prioritized target lists.
Business Impact High

FOUNDATIONAL: Unlocks Playbook and Briefing Agents. Precision targeting. Every MCC domain needs this.

Time Savings
  • CXO team: ad hoc lookups. All Named Account FMs/DSs/sellers benefit.
Future Extensions & Reusability
  • EXTREMELY HIGH: Foundation for all agents, events, outbound, sales, account planning.
  • CDO non-negotiable. CIO for dev. 2,200 accounts x 8+ roles.
Feasibility Medium
  • Rev Tech connected sources. Risks: accuracy maintenance; Geo/BU; seller adoption; CDO not initiated.
  • [RISK: CDO partnership not yet initiated]
Primary Friction Points
  • 1. ISC frequently inaccurate
  • 2. Manual searching; months for 400-500 accounts
  • 3. Geo/Global/BU complexity
  • 4. Sellers don't update ISC
  • 5. No automated monitoring
  • 6. Stale cleanup neglected
  • 7. AI tools inadequate
Technical Requirements
Data Sources
  • ISC, IDM, TAP 360, ZoomInfo/Cognism/Lusha, LinkedIn, Copilot, Spreadsheets
  • [OPEN: Geo/BU disambiguation logic?]
  • [OPEN: CDO pipeline architecture?]
System / Integration Requirements
  • Continuous monitoring. Multi-source corroboration. Seller notification. CDO pipeline. Geo/BU disambiguation. Contact lifecycle.
Candidate Vendors / Tools
  • ZoomInfo, Cognism, Lusha (Rev Tech). CDO office essential.
Other Dependencies & Open Items
  • CRITICAL: CDO partnership; Rev Tech coordination; seller adoption.
  • HIGH: LinkedIn; Geo/BU complexity.
  • MEDIUM: ISC cleanup backlog.
  • 1. Seller notification mechanism
  • 2. Geo/BU logic
  • 3. CDO pipeline architecture
  • 4. Baseline accuracy rate
KPI's
  • CXO record accuracy rate (current: ~30-40%; target: >90%)
  • Time to validate/update a contact record (current: manual; target: auto)
  • % of outbound campaigns with verified contact data
Growth Impact
Foundation for all agents, events, outbound, sales, account planning
Productivity Impact
Operational efficiency gains
Discovery Gaps 15 gaps
All identified gaps for this workflow requiring follow-up investigation or resolution

IBM Consulting / © 2026 IBM Corporation | MCC & IBM Confidential C-Suite Contact Accuracy & Account Targeting Agent  |  Workflow Blueprint
Grant Lifecycle Orchestrator Agent
CSR
$75M giving commitment. Staff manually check 3-4 systems per grant (BVD, DPL, Salesforce, RCI). Christian: 40-50% of team time on grant compliance. CSR classified high-risk in IBM
#1
Brief Description

Orchestrates the full IBM CSR grant lifecycle from partner application through compliance validation, milestone monitoring, payment qualification, and audit trail generation across Versaic, Salesforce, and compliance systems.

Process Owners
  • Christian Schoen
  • Rachel Mohammed
  • Justina Nixon-Saintil
  • Grant admin
  • CSRMs
  • Benevity/Versaic
  • RCI
  • IBM Audit
  • Finance
User Groups
  • Grant admin: Compliance checks
  • CSRMs: Partner relationships
  • RCI: Mandated reviews
  • Finance: Payments
  • Audit: Oversight
Future State: What AI Does
AI-Enabled Workflow
  • QUALIFY: Auto-run BVD, DPL, RCI, board member checks on application.
  • MONITOR: Track milestones vs. SkillsBuild data; auto-reconcile.
  • DETECT: Flag off-track grants via variance.
  • REPORT: Audit-ready documentation.
  • ESCALATE: Route flagged grants.
  • ASKCSR: Conversational guidance for CSRMs.
Business Impact Medium

HIGH. Supports $75M commitment. 40-50% team time reclaimable. High-risk audit area. Justina: 'not under my oversight have a penalty.' Speeds grant pipeline. Frees CSRMs for partner engagement.

Time Savings
  • Christian's grant admin (40-50% of time). All CSRMs. Audit, finance, RCI. University partners (Lydia: affected cross-team).
Future Extensions & Reusability
  • MEDIUM: Grant pattern CSR-specific but multi-system compliance orchestration applies broadly. Paul drew parallel to ecosystem partner agent (17 data sources).
  • Benevity partnership for APIs. CIO for pipeline. RCI for handoff. Finance for payment. Audit for validation.
Feasibility Medium
  • Multiple systems need integration (Versaic, BVD, DPL, Salesforce). Some automation must be done by Benevity. Structured compliance rules. Paul: data pipeline approach over tool-to-tool.
  • [RISK: Benevity API status unclear — milestone tracking due June]
Primary Friction Points
  • 1. Manual multi-system compliance checking per grant (BVD, DPL, Salesforce, RCI)
  • 2. Tool switching across IBM + third-party systems
  • 3. RCI reviews external to CSR but gate progression
  • 4. No single source of truth for partners (Lydia: '3 different tools')
  • 5. Progress report reconciliation manual
  • 6. Country-specific clip levels (Korea: $0)
Technical Requirements
Data Sources
  • Versaic (Benevity), BVD, DPL, Salesforce, CSR Analytics/Tableau, SkillsBuild, RCI Systems, Finance/SAP
  • [OPEN: single macro orchestrator or phased micro agents?]
  • [RISK: RCI external process — automation feasibility unknown]
System / Integration Requirements
  • Data pipeline: BVD+DPL+board member DBs -> Versaic. Salesforce API. SkillsBuild data feed. Auto audit trail. AskCSR conversational interface.
Candidate Vendors / Tools
  • Versaic/Benevity (external vendor), BVD, DPL, Salesforce, watsonx.ai/orchestrate, Data pipeline approach (Paul)
Other Dependencies & Open Items
  • CRITICAL: Benevity/Versaic API capabilities; RCI external process.
  • HIGH: Audit framework alignment; multi-system integration across org boundaries.
  • MEDIUM: Partner capacity (small nonprofits); country-specific rules.
  • 1. Annual grant volume/timeline
  • 2. Grant admin FTE count
  • 3. Manual lookups per grant
  • 4. Board member check process
  • 5. Versaic/Benevity API capabilities
KPI's
  • Reduction in manual reconciliation time (hrs/grant/cycle)
  • % of grants with automated milestone tracking (target: 100%)
  • Milestone-to-report turnaround (current: days; target: same day)
Growth Impact
Grant pattern CSR-specific but multi-system compliance orchestration applies broadly
Productivity Impact
40-50% team time reclaimable
Discovery Gaps 13 gaps
All identified gaps for this workflow requiring follow-up investigation or resolution

SkillsBuild Partner Onboarding & Lifecycle Agent
CSR
1,000+ global partners (universities, nonprofits, high schools) for 30M skills goal. No single source of truth for partners. Translation outsourced to vendors (Stryker); competitor
#2
Brief Description

Manages the end-to-end partner lifecycle for IBM SkillsBuild from initial inquiry through onboarding, compliance validation, content delivery, translation, and renewal across universities, nonprofits, and high schools.

Process Owners
  • Lydia Logan
  • Kate (onboarding)
  • Sonia (content)
  • Rachel Mohammed
  • Leslie Hernandez
  • CSRMs
  • Partners
User Groups
  • Kate: Onboarding
  • CSRMs: Relationships
  • Sonia: Content/curriculum
  • Leslie: Marketing
  • Translation vendors: Localization
Future State: What AI Does
AI-Enabled Workflow
  • ONBOARD: Auto compliance screening (shared with Grant agent). Guide agreement/provisioning.
  • TRANSLATE: AI curriculum translation with human QA.
  • MONITOR: Engaged learner milestones across 1,000+ partners.
  • TRACK: Marketing activation per partner.
  • RENEW: Qualification based on milestones.
Business Impact Medium

HIGH. Supports 30M skills goal. 1,000+ partners benefit. Lydia: 'impact across basically all partners.' Translation competitive gap. Partner visibility compounds all workflows.

Time Savings
  • Kate's onboarding team, CSRMs globally, Sonia's content team, Leslie's marketing. All 1,000+ partner organizations.
Future Extensions & Reusability
  • MEDIUM: Compliance screening shared with Grant agent. Translation capability for any MCC multi-language content. CRM layer benefits all CSR.
  • Benevity for platform. Translation vendor assessment. CIO for CRM/Salesforce. SkillsBuild platform team.
Feasibility Medium
  • Kate already improving onboarding (foundation). Compliance shared with Grant agent. Risks: translation quality for academic content; video translation; outsourced development workflows; Benevity dependency.
  • [RISK: translation quality bar for academic curriculum]
  • [RISK: Benevity platform dependency]

  • 1. Partner history across multiple systems; no CRM
  • 2. No single source of truth (Lydia: '3 different tools, may not be there at all')
  • 3. Translation cost/speed bottleneck (competitors faster)
  • 4. Cross-team: CSRMs, grant admin, content, marketing, vendors
  • 5. Same multi-system compliance as grant lifecycle
  • 6. Monitoring 1,000+ partners labor-intensive
Technical Requirements
Data Sources
  • SkillsBuild, Versaic, CSR Analytics/Tableau, Translation Vendors, Marketing Tools, BVD/DPL/Salesforce
  • [OPEN: AI translation quality for academic content?]
  • [OPEN: video translation approach?]
System / Integration Requirements
  • Shared compliance with Grant agent. CRM/Salesforce integration. AI translation pipeline (text+video). Partner engagement dashboard. Marketing tracking.
Candidate Vendors / Tools
  • SkillsBuild Platform, Versaic/Benevity, Translation vendors (Stryker), AI translation tools TBD, CSR Analytics
Other Dependencies & Open Items
  • CRITICAL: Translation quality bar (academic curriculum); Benevity platform.
  • HIGH: CRM/single source of truth; shared compliance infrastructure.
  • MEDIUM: Video translation; outsourced development workflows.
  • 1. Annual onboardings/timeline
  • 2. Translation spend/language breakdown
  • 3. Kate's current scope
  • 4. Content development workflow
  • 5. AI translation quality for academic content
KPI's
  • Partner onboarding cycle time (current: weeks; target: <5 days)
  • % of onboarding steps completed without manual intervention
  • Translation turnaround per language (current: weeks; target: <48 hrs)
Growth Impact
Compliance screening shared with Grant agent
Productivity Impact
Onboarding time reduction

Volunteer & Giving Operations Agent
CSR
4M volunteer hours target. ~90,000 employees engage (30% of 300K). Sara's team handles high inquiry volumes (email, Slack). Benevity platform not always intuitive. Justina's vision
#3
Brief Description

Streamlines IBM's employee volunteerism and giving programs by enabling employees to log hours, submit donations, and navigate the Benevity platform through a conversational interface while automating inquiry triage, approval routing, and matching gift processing.

Process Owners
  • Justina Nixon-Saintil
  • Sara Link
  • Rachel Mohammed
  • ~90
  • 000 employees
  • Benevity
User Groups
  • Sara's team: Inquiry handling
  • Employees: End users
  • Rachel: Operations
  • Benevity: Platform
Future State: What AI Does
AI-Enabled Workflow
  • CONVERSE: Ask HR-style agent for volunteer/giving.
  • VALIDATE: Organization compliance check.
  • ROUTE: Approval with context.
  • PROCESS: Log hours, donations, matching.
  • TRIAGE: FAQ/inquiry first-line.
  • ESCALATE: Complex to Sara's team.
Business Impact Medium

MEDIUM-HIGH. Supports 4M hours goal. Every friction point discourages participation and leaves hours unreported. Fundamentally improves UX. Frees Sara's team for program management.

Time Savings

#3
Brief Description

Identifies underpenetrated geographies, segments, and accounts by combining pipeline gap analysis with propensity scoring and firmographic data, then recommends specific next-best-action plays tailored to the nature of each gap.

Process Owners
  • Dario Munoz (VP Analytics)
  • Sadique Khan (Field Analytics)
  • Romi Ravi (TAP 360)
  • Alli McGugan (Demand Insights)
  • David Bush (Analytics Leader)

  • Dario: Strategic vision
  • Sadique: Pipeline analysis, account insights

  • Go leaders: Consume recommendations
  • Demand teams: Execute activation
Future State: What AI Does
AI-Enabled Workflow
  • DETECT: Monitor pipeline against targets across Geo × segment × product.
  • CLASSIFY: Gap type — not progressing, insufficient, or nonexistent.
  • SCORE: Overlay propensity-to-buy on accounts in gap areas.
  • RECOMMEND: Next-best-action by gap type (progression, creation, awareness).
  • ANALYZE: Buying group completeness for priority accounts.
  • BRIEF: Generate account/segment opportunity briefs.
  • ROUTE: Connect recommendations to demand teams and activation channels.

Dario: 'If you tell me I have these gaps in pipeline in this geo, what accounts have propensity indicators to close the gap.' Team's strategic 'Nirvana' aspiration beyond day-to-day automation.

Buyer and Account Intelligence Agent
Named Demand Strategy
Continuously assembles and refreshes unified buyer and account profiles by joining 1P behavioral data, firmographic and technographic signals, and 3P intent data. Dynamically re-se
#1
Brief Description

Continuously assembles and refreshes unified buyer and account profiles by joining first-party behavioral data, firmographic/technographic signals, and third-party intent data, dynamically re-segmenting accounts and flagging those crossing intent thresholds for campaign activation.

Process Owners
  • Claudia Masseo
  • Vanina Marcote
  • Vijaysanthi (Shanti) Ramanathan
  • Priscilla Kim
  • Sachiko Tsuchiya
  • Romy / Ravi (Insights Navigator team)
  • Sales leadership (unnamed)
User Groups
  • Claudia Masseo: Named Demand Strategy lead, growth cohort definition
  • Vanina Marcote: Buying group optimization, account-level execution
  • Vijaysanthi (Shanti) Ramanathan: India/South Asia market demand strategy, child entity mapping
  • Priscilla Kim: Global demand strategy leadership, sales-marketing integration
  • Sachiko Tsuchiya: Japan market demand strategy, buying group confidence
  • Romy / Ravi (Insights Navigator team): Tab 360 / Tableau data owners
  • Sales leadership: Account plan owners, Horizon account prioritization
Future State: What AI Does
AI-Enabled Workflow
  • Data Ingestion & Unification: Agent pulls 1P behavioral data from ISC/EPM, 3P intent signals (Bombora), firmographic and technographic data from Insights Navigator (Tab 360/Tableau), and content syndication response data from paid media agencies. Resolves entity mismatches across parent/child hierarchies.
  • Entity Resolution & Hierarchy Mapping: Agent reconciles duplicate and mismatched records across systems (e.g., Shanti's example: same CTO tagged as 'Aditya Birla Capital' in LinkedIn, 'Aditya Birla Renewable Solar Limited' in ISC, and 'Aditya Birla Management' in EPM). Maps child entities to parent accounts with confidence scoring. [GAP] What is the current scale of entity mismatches? How many named accounts have known child-entity data quality issues?
  • ICP Scoring & Segmentation: Agent computes and refreshes Ideal Customer Profile scores using combined signals. Dynamically segments accounts into growth cohorts based on intent patterns, engagement history, install base, and pipeline status.
  • Buying Group Assembly: Agent identifies individuals within accounts engaging with IBM content, maps them to buying group roles (minimum 4 per UT17 level), and scores buying group completeness. Flags groups needing additional role coverage.
  • Threshold Alerting: When accounts cross intent or engagement thresholds, agent surfaces alerts to demand planners and field marketers with recommended next actions.
  • Output Distribution: Unified account profiles, buying group status, and prioritized account lists are published to demand planning tools, AJO/AEP for activation, and field marketing dashboards. [GAP] What is the target delivery format — dashboard, automated email digest, AEP audience push, or all of the above?
  • Continuous Refresh: Agent monitors for new signals and re-scores continuously rather than on planning cycle cadence, transforming account intelligence from periodic to always-on.
  • ☑ Insight generation: Core capability. Agent synthesizes 1P behavioral, 3P intent, firmographic, and technographic signals into unified account intelligence with ICP scores, buying group completeness metrics, and growth cohort recommendations. Replaces manual Insights Navigator lookups and cross-system data aggregation.
  • ☑ Drafting / content generation: [NOT APPLICABLE] — This agent produces data outputs and recommendations, not content drafts.
  • ☑ Risk scoring / pre-review: Agent scores buying group confidence levels (addressing Sachiko's concern about inability to tell sellers 'with confidence' whether groups are real buying groups vs. scattered individuals). Flags entity mismatches and data quality issues before they propagate to activation.
  • ☑ Executive summarization: Generates account-level and cohort-level summary views for demand planners, replacing manual dashboard assembly.
  • ☑ Workflow automation: Automates the end-to-end data assembly pipeline that currently precedes every planning cycle and ABM campaign targeting exercise — the single most time-consuming manual step in the Named Demand workflow.
  • Hypothesis: An AI agent that continuously unifies and scores account data across IBM's fragmented system landscape would eliminate the largest manual bottleneck in Named Demand Strategy. By replacing the periodic, labor-intensive data assembly cycle with a continuously refreshed intelligence layer, the agent would free demand planners to focus on strategy and activation rather than data wrangling. The buying group confidence scoring directly addresses the team's inability to provide sellers with reliable buying group intelligence.
  • Conversational Refinement Note: The team's discussion heavily emphasized entity resolution challenges (child entity mismatches across ISC, EPM, and LinkedIn) and buying group confidence. The Adobe capability review underway with David Gerken's team may overlap with some audience segmentation functions — the agent design should be validated against Adobe AEP/AJO capabilities to avoid duplication.
Business Impact High

HIGH. Profile assembly is the primary bottleneck preceding every planning cycle and ABM activation. Vanina: '70% of my team's time' on buying group work. Claudia: growth cohort list pulling 'takes more work than it probably should.' Eliminating this bottleneck would transform Named Demand from react

Demand Planning Orchestration Agent
Named Demand Strategy
On planning cycle trigger, collects and synthesizes all planning inputs including historicals, pipeline data, macro signals, capacity constraints, and financial targets into a stru
#2
Brief Description

Collects and synthesizes all planning inputs—historicals, pipeline data, macro signals, capacity constraints, and financial targets—into a structured demand plan draft, allocates budget and target recommendations across channels and geos, and routes for approval and publication.

Process Owners
  • Claudia Masseo
  • Vanina Marcote
  • Priscilla Kim
  • Vijaysanthi (Shanti) Ramanathan
  • Sachiko Tsuchiya
  • Finance / IPA tool owners
User Groups
  • Claudia Masseo: Named Demand Strategy lead, budget allocation decisions Vanina Marcote: Growth cohort planning, buying group targets Priscilla Kim: Global demand strategy, geo-market alignment, forecast methodology Vijaysanthi (Shanti) Ramanathan: India/South Asia market planning, child entity allocation Sachiko Tsuchiya: Japan market planning, campaign launch coordination Finance / IPA tool owners: Forecast input and pipeline prediction
Future State: What AI Does
AI-Enabled Workflow
  • Planning Trigger & Input Collection: On cycle start, agent collects historical performance data, current pipeline status, financial targets, capacity constraints, and macro market signals from ISC, EPM, IPA, and Salesforce.
  • Geo & Market Input Aggregation: Agent solicits and aggregates inputs from geo markets (priority industries, account focus areas, capacity). Currently done via 'email or Excel' (Claudia). [GAP] How many geos submit planning inputs and what is the typical turnaround time?
  • Draft Plan Generation: Agent synthesizes inputs into a structured demand plan with budget allocation recommendations across channels, geos, and teams. Uses historical performance patterns and current pipeline signals to inform allocations.
  • Target Setting & Forecasting: Agent generates pipeline and win revenue forecasts using historical attribution data and performance patterns. Addresses Priscilla's concern that current forecasting is 'not based on any sort of predictive or AI-enabled methodology' but rather individual judgment.
  • Stakeholder Review & Routing: Draft plan is routed to relevant stakeholders for review and approval. Agent tracks sign-off status and escalates delays.
  • Plan Publication & System Distribution: Approved plan is published to relevant execution systems (Marketo, AJO, paid media platforms) and geo teams for activation.
  • Continuous Monitoring & Reforecast: Agent monitors plan performance against targets and triggers mid-cycle reforecast recommendations when significant deviations are detected.
  • ☑ Insight generation: Agent synthesizes historical performance, pipeline data, and macro signals into planning recommendations. Addresses Priscilla's call for more data-driven planning: 'if we're going to spend so much time looking at optimization, we also need to be really thoughtful about how we predict and forecast.'
  • ☑ Drafting / content generation: Generates structured demand plan drafts with budget allocations, channel mix recommendations, and target setting. Replaces manual plan assembly.
  • ☑ Risk scoring / pre-review: Identifies allocation risks — channels or geos where historical performance suggests targets may be unrealistic. Flags capacity constraints against plan ambitions.
  • ☑ Anomaly detection: Detects mid-cycle deviations from plan and triggers reforecast recommendations. Identifies outlier performance patterns across geos.
  • ☑ Executive summarization: Generates planning cycle summaries for leadership review, including forecast confidence levels and key assumption documentation.
  • ☑ Workflow automation: Automates the end-to-end planning input collection, synthesis, and distribution process that currently consumes the early weeks of every planning cycle.
  • Hypothesis: An AI-driven planning orchestration agent would transform the demand planning cycle from a weeks-long manual data collection and synthesis exercise into a rapid, data-driven process. By automating input aggregation, applying predictive analytics to forecast generation, and orchestrating the approval and distribution workflow, the agent would compress cycle time and improve forecast accuracy. The current state — where pipeline forecasts are based on individual judgment rather than data-driven methodology — represents a significant opportunity for AI-enabled improvement.
  • Conversational Refinement Note: Priscilla specifically called out IPA forecast methodology as an area for improvement. David Gerken connected this to David Bush's attribution work, which could inform predictive forecasting. The agent design should incorporate attribution-derived patterns where available.
Business Impact High

HIGH. The planning cycle is 'the primary unit of work' for Named Demand (screenshot). Compressing cycle time means faster time-to-activation for campaigns. Improved forecast accuracy means better budget allocation and more credible marketing contribution metrics.

  • Content & Messaging Strategy: Content planning cycles could use similar input aggregation and approval routing

  • Attribution / Analytics (David Bush team): Predictive forecasting component creates a feedback loop with attribution data

  • MODERATE. Requires integration with IPA, EPM, ISC, and Salesforce for input data. Predictive forecasting layer requires historical attribution data (David Bush team dependency). Plan routing/approval is a standard workflow automation pattern. [GAP] Is historical attribution data available in a structured format that could feed a predictive model?

ABM Account Intelligence and Campaign Activation Agent
Named Demand Strategy
For a defined set of named accounts, pulls account activity signals, competitive intelligence, and buyer journey stage indicators, generates a prioritized account action list with
#3
Brief Description

Pulls account activity signals, competitive intelligence, and buyer journey indicators for named accounts, generates a prioritized action list with recommended campaign plays, drafts account-specific content variants, and routes activation triggers to field marketing or sellers.

Process Owners
  • Claudia Masseo
  • Vanina Marcote
  • Vijaysanthi (Shanti) Ramanathan
  • Priscilla Kim
  • Field marketing teams (geo-level)
  • Sales teams
  • Content & Messaging Strategy team
User Groups
  • Claudia Masseo: Growth cohort definition, ABM strategy, Faris IQ vendor evaluation Vanina Marcote: Account-level execution, buying group engagement Vijaysanthi (Shanti) Ramanathan: India market ABM execution, child entity activation Priscilla Kim: Global ABM strategy, sales-marketing integration Field marketing teams (geo-level): Activation execution recipients Sales teams: Account plan owners, pipeline intelligence providers Content & Messaging Strategy team: Campaign content providers
Future State: What AI Does
AI-Enabled Workflow
  • Signal Monitoring: Agent continuously monitors account activity signals across 1P engagement data (email, web, events), 3P intent (Bombora), competitive intelligence (Faris IQ), and pipeline movement (Salesforce/ISC).
  • Account Scoring & Prioritization: Agent scores accounts based on engagement intensity, buying group completeness, pipeline stage, and competitive threat level. Generates prioritized activation list with rationale.
  • Campaign Play Recommendation: Based on account status and signals, agent recommends specific campaign plays (e.g., CFO roundtable, content syndication push, field event). Matches account needs to available campaign assets and channels.
  • Content & Messaging Drafting: Agent drafts account-specific content variants and messaging recommendations based on account firmographics, industry, engagement history, and competitive context. [GAP] What is the current content personalization capability? How many message variants does the team typically produce per campaign?
  • Activation Routing: Agent routes activation triggers to the appropriate field marketing team or seller based on account ownership, geo, and campaign type. Includes recommended next actions and supporting intelligence.
  • Competitive Threat Integration: Agent connects competitive intelligence (Faris IQ outside-in data, market signals) to tactical campaign adjustments in real-time rather than as separate planning exercises.
  • Performance Feedback Loop: Agent tracks activation outcomes and feeds results back into scoring and recommendation models for continuous improvement.
  • ☑ Insight generation: Core capability. Agent synthesizes account signals across multiple sources to generate actionable account intelligence and campaign play recommendations. Addresses Claudia's vision: 'there would be something that triggers — these accounts are clearly showing similar patterns... here are the next best actions.'
  • ☑ Drafting / content generation: Agent drafts account-specific content variants and messaging recommendations tailored to industry, persona, competitive context, and engagement stage.
  • ☑ Risk scoring / pre-review: Scores competitive threat levels and flags accounts at risk of competitive displacement based on Faris IQ and other signals.
  • ☑ Anomaly detection: Detects unusual engagement patterns (sudden drop-off, competitive signal spikes) and triggers proactive outreach recommendations.
  • ☑ Orchestration / routing: Routes activation triggers to appropriate field marketing teams and sellers based on account ownership and recommended play type.
  • ☑ Executive summarization: Generates account-level and cohort-level activation summaries for global and geo leadership.
  • ☑ Workflow automation: Automates the signal-to-activation pipeline that currently requires manual cross-referencing of multiple data sources, manual list building, and manual routing to field teams.
  • Hypothesis: An ABM activation agent would transform Named Demand from periodic, campaign-driven account marketing to continuous, signal-driven activation. By connecting competitive intelligence directly to tactical campaign plays and automating the routing to field teams, the agent would make ABM execution systematic at scale. Claudia's vision — 'almost all of it could be automated at some point... something that triggers next best actions' — describes an achievable near-term state where AI handles signal processing, recommendation, and routing while humans validate and execute.
  • Conversational Refinement Note: This workflow bridges Workflows 1 (intelligence) and 2 (planning) by translating unified account intelligence into account-level activation. The team identified it as a 'Team Workflow (micro) / Workflow (macro)' indicating it can start as account-level micro-activations and scale to full macro workflow. Claudia flagged Faris IQ as a key vendor for outside-in competitive data that would differentiate this agent.
Business Impact High

HIGH. ABM at named account scale requires account-specific intelligence and activation speed that manual processes cannot sustain across a large account universe (screenshot). Systematic ABM execution would directly increase pipeline contribution and buying group formation rates.

Customer Story and Reference Curation Agent
Named Demand Strategy
Monitors the IBM customer story library and external signals including press releases, case studies, and analyst coverage for new or updated references relevant to defined solution
#4
Brief Description

Monitors IBM's customer story library and external signals for new or updated references relevant to defined solution areas, generates draft story summaries in approved IBM format, routes for approval, and surfaces the most relevant references at the point of campaign activation or meeting preparation.

Process Owners
  • Customer Story and Sales Enablement team
  • Legal / compliance
  • Analyst relations
  • Sellers and field marketers
  • Named Demand Strategy team
User Groups
  • Customer Story and Sales Enablement team: Primary owners of reference library Legal / compliance: Approval authority for customer story publication
  • Analyst relations: Source of analyst coverage and mentions
  • Sellers and field marketers: Reference consumers at point of need Named Demand Strategy team: Campaign-level reference matching
Future State: What AI Does
AI-Enabled Workflow
  • Signal Monitoring: Agent monitors internal sources (CRM win notifications, press release queue, customer success reports) and external sources (press coverage, analyst reports, social media) for new or updated customer stories.
  • Story Identification & Drafting: Agent identifies stories relevant to defined solution areas and buyer personas. Generates draft summaries in approved IBM format with key talking points, metrics, and use case details. [GAP] What is the current IBM-approved customer story format and template?
  • Approval Routing: Agent routes draft stories to customer and legal approval queues with pre-populated approval forms. Tracks approval status and escalates delays.
  • Library Update: Approved stories are automatically cataloged in the reference library with metadata tags (industry, solution area, persona, geography, date, metrics).
  • Reference Matching: When campaigns are activated or sellers request references, agent matches the most relevant stories based on account context (industry, solution needs, competitive situation) and surfaces them at point of need.
  • Freshness Monitoring: Agent flags stories approaching expiration (metrics becoming dated, customer relationship changes) and triggers refresh workflows.
  • ☑ Insight generation: Agent identifies which customer stories are most relevant to specific accounts, industries, and competitive situations based on contextual matching.
  • ☑ Drafting / content generation: Core capability. Agent generates draft customer story summaries in approved IBM format from raw inputs (press releases, case studies, win reports). Reduces manual drafting time.
  • ☑ Risk scoring / pre-review: Flags potential compliance or sensitivity issues before routing for approval (e.g., customer in regulated industry, NDA constraints).
  • ☑ Executive summarization: Generates summary views of reference library coverage by industry, solution area, and geography — identifies gaps in coverage.
  • ☑ Workflow automation: Automates the end-to-end story lifecycle from detection through drafting, approval, publication, and retirement.
  • Hypothesis: A customer story curation agent would transform the reference function from a reactive, manually maintained library to a proactive, continuously updated intelligence asset. By automatically monitoring for new stories, drafting summaries, managing approvals, and matching references to accounts at point of need, the agent ensures sellers always have current, relevant proof points. The shift from manual identification and bottlenecked approval cycles to automated curation would directly accelerate deal progression in named accounts.
Business Impact High

MODERATE. Accelerates deal progression by ensuring relevant proof points are available at point of need. Directly supports ABM activation (Workflow 3) with account-appropriate references. [GAP] What is the estimated impact of having timely, relevant customer references on deal close rates?

Future Extensions & Reusability
  • All MCC domains: Customer story library is a shared asset consumed across all marketing functions
  • Sales enablement: Reference matching directly supports seller meeting preparation and proposal development
  • Content & Messaging Strategy: Customer stories are a content type that feeds into campaign creation
  • C-Suite Experience & ABM: Executive engagement briefings require curated, relevant customer proof points
  • Innovation Studio: Client experience demonstrations benefit from current, relevant case studies
Feasibility High
  • HIGH. Story drafting from structured inputs is a well-suited LLM task. Monitoring external signals is a standard NLP/scraping pattern. Approval routing is standard workflow automation. Reference matching uses established recommendation/search patterns. [GAP] Are there existing content management APIs that the agent can integrate with for library management?
Primary Friction Points
  • 1. Manual identification and curation: Customer story curation is 'currently reactive and bottlenecked on manual identification and approval cycles' (screenshot).
  • 2. Approval cycle delays: Customer and legal approval workflows create bottlenecks between story identification and publication.
  • 3. Reference matching at point of need: Sellers and field marketers need the right reference at the right moment (campaign activation, meeting prep) but discovery is manual.

  • Salesforce: Win notifications, account context for reference matching

  • Seller advisory group: Understand reference consumption patterns and unmet needs

  • New Tech Requirements
  • External signal monitoring: Press release, analyst report, and social media monitoring for customer mentions
  • Story drafting engine: LLM-based generation of story summaries in IBM-approved format
Other Dependencies & Open Items
  • Customer approval: Every story requires customer permission for external use — this is a non-automatable human-in-the-loop step
  • Legal review requirements: Compliance review may have mandatory human review requirements that limit automation of the approval stage
  • Story format standardization: Agent drafting requires a consistent, well-defined template — if current stories are ad hoc, template standardization is a prerequisite
  • External monitoring access: Press and analyst monitoring may require additional tool licensing (Meltwater, etc.)
  • CRM data quality: Win notifications from Salesforce depend on opportunity data quality and timely stage updates

Campaign Performance Intelligence and Optimization Agent
Named Demand Strategy
Tracks plan versus actual demand performance on a defined cadence, generates performance summary reports for demand marketers and leadership, identifies underperforming campaign in
#5
Brief Description

Tracks plan-versus-actual demand performance, identifies underperforming campaign investments using statistical significance thresholds, generates budget reallocation recommendations with supporting rationale, and routes approved reallocations to campaign and finance systems.

Process Owners
  • Claudia Masseo
  • Priscilla Kim
  • Vanina Marcote
  • Vijaysanthi (Shanti) Ramanathan
  • Sachiko Tsuchiya
  • David Bush and attribution team
  • Finance / budget owners
User Groups
  • Claudia Masseo: Campaign strategy, budget ownership Priscilla Kim: Global performance oversight, forecast accuracy, feedback loop optimization Vanina Marcote: Campaign execution performance Vijaysanthi (Shanti) Ramanathan: Market-level campaign performance, India/South Asia Sachiko Tsuchiya: Japan market campaign performance David Bush and attribution team: Performance measurement methodology
  • Finance / budget owners: Reallocation approval authority
Future State: What AI Does
AI-Enabled Workflow
  • Performance Data Ingestion: Agent collects campaign performance data from EPM, CJA, AJO, paid media platforms, and attribution models. Aggregates plan vs. actual metrics across all active campaigns, channels, and geos.
  • Statistical Analysis & Signal Detection: Agent applies statistical significance testing to identify campaigns genuinely underperforming vs. normal variance. Flags campaigns crossing defined thresholds.
  • Performance Report Generation: Agent generates standardized performance summary reports for demand marketers and leadership with key metrics, trend analysis, and performance vs. plan comparisons.
  • Reallocation Recommendation: For underperforming campaigns, agent generates budget reallocation recommendations with supporting rationale — where to shift budget, expected impact, and confidence level based on historical patterns.
  • Global-Geo Feedback Synthesis: Agent aggregates performance signals from geos and synthesizes global performance view. Addresses Priscilla's desire to 'automate the feedback loop in a real-time way' between global and markets.
  • Approval & Execution Routing: Reallocation recommendations are routed to appropriate approvers based on budget authority levels. Upon approval, adjustments are published to campaign and finance systems.
  • Forecast Accuracy Tracking: Agent compares original forecasts to actual outcomes, tracks forecast accuracy over time, and improves predictive models based on observed patterns.
  • ☑ Insight generation: Core capability. Agent synthesizes performance data across channels, geos, and campaigns to identify optimization opportunities. Generates attribution-informed insights about what's working and what's not.
  • ☑ Drafting / content generation: Generates standardized performance reports and reallocation recommendation memos with supporting rationale.
  • ☑ Anomaly detection: Detects performance anomalies — campaigns performing significantly above or below expectations — and surfaces for investigation.
  • ☑ Orchestration / routing: Routes reallocation recommendations through approval workflow and publishes approved changes to campaign and finance systems.
  • ☑ Executive summarization: Generates leadership-ready performance summaries with key metrics, trends, and recommended actions. Addresses Priscilla's need for 'real-time feedback' between global and geos.
  • ☑ Workflow automation: Automates the manual analysis, report generation, and reallocation recommendation process that currently spans weeks and multiple stakeholder review cycles.
  • Hypothesis: A campaign performance optimization agent would close the latency gap between performance signal and budget action that is a structural constraint in the current model. By automating signal detection through statistical analysis, generating reallocation recommendations with rationale, and routing approvals efficiently, the agent would compress the optimization cycle from weeks to days. Priscilla's call for predictive outcome forecasting and automated geo-global feedback loops describes exactly what this agent would deliver — a continuous, data-driven optimization engine that replaces periodic manual review.
  • Conversational Refinement Note: Priscilla's two specific requests — automated feedback loops between global and geos, and predictive outcome forecasting — are both core to this workflow. Automated RFI Response Development and Fact Review Agent
Social Media & Influence
An agentic workflow that automates the generation of RFI (Request for Information) responses and supports fact review of evaluative analyst reports, targeting at least 50% automati
#1
Brief Description

Automates the generation of RFI responses and fact review of evaluative analyst reports, targeting at least 50% automation of RFI production with analyst-ready draft answers produced in minutes.

Future State: What AI Does
AI-Enabled Workflow
  • Incoming RFI or evaluative report is received and ingested by the agent from analyst firm portal or email
  • Agent parses the RFI structure, identifies question categories, and matches against the internal Fact Review and RFI report database
  • Agent generates draft responses by synthesizing approved messaging, prior RFI answers, CEO Repository content, and product documentation
  • Draft responses are auto-scored for confidence level; high-confidence answers are flagged as analyst-ready, lower-confidence answers are routed for SME review
  • Human reviewer validates draft answers, makes edits, and approves final responses
  • Approved responses are submitted to the analyst firm and archived in the RFI database for future reuse
  • Agent captures feedback on draft quality to improve future response generation
AI Capabilities
  • ☑ Insight generation: Analyze patterns across historical RFI responses to identify frequently asked questions and optimal answer templates
  • ☑ Drafting / content generation: Generate analyst-ready draft RFI responses synthesized from approved sources, prior answers, and product documentation
  • ☑ Risk scoring / pre-review: Score draft responses for accuracy confidence and flag claims requiring human verification
  • ☑ Orchestration / routing: Route low-confidence answers to appropriate SMEs while auto-approving high-confidence responses
  • ☑ Executive summarization: Synthesize multi-source inputs into concise, analyst-ready response narratives
  • ☑ Workflow automation: Automate at least 50% of RFI production end-to-end with minimal human intervention
Hypothesis
  • An RFI Response Agent would leverage IBM's existing Fact Review and RFI database as a knowledge foundation, applying LLM-driven synthesis to produce draft responses that match the quality and specificity analysts expect. The agent would learn from prior approved responses, progressively improving co
Business Impact High

The CAB Wishlist targets 50% automation of RFI production — a quantified goal indicating significant current manual burden. [GAP] What is the current average RFI turnaround time, and how many RFIs are processed annually?

Future Extensions & Reusability
  • RFI response patterns directly reusable for any IBM domain fielding analyst inquiries (product marketing, infrastructure, consulting)
  • Fact review engine reusable for executive communications consistency checking (see Workflow 2: Automated Fact Review)
  • Draft synthesis patterns applicable to competitive intelligence responses and customer proposal generation
  • Knowledge base architecture reusable across the Unified Corporate Affairs Knowledge & Reputation Lens (Workflow 4)
Feasibility Low
  • Requires mature, structured RFI archive — if this does not exist, foundational data work is prerequisite
  • LLM model selection and deployment (watsonx vs. third-party)
  • Legal/compliance review of AI-generated content for analyst-facing outputs
New Tech Required
  • LLM with retrieval-augmented generation (RAG) capabilities
  • Structured RFI database with semantic search
  • API integration with analyst firm portals (if available)
  • Confidence scoring and human-in-the-loop approval workflow
Primary Friction Points
  • 1. Manual RFI response synthesis across multiple sources and SME consultations
  • 2. Content scattered across CEO Repository, product docs, prior RFIs, and SME knowledge
  • 3. Handoff / coordination delays between AR team, SMEs, and reviewers
  • 4. Prior RFI responses not systematically archived or easily searchable
  • 5. High volume of RFIs across multiple analyst firms creates capacity constraints
Technical Requirements
Engagement Needed
  • CIO partnership for LLM integration and RAG architecture
  • AR organization engagement for RFI database structuring and quality validation
Additional Discovery
  • Inventory of existing RFI database: format, completeness, searchability
  • Current RFI volume, turnaround time, and staffing model
  • SME consultation patterns: which groups are most frequently engaged?
Dependencies & Constraints
  • Requires mature, structured RFI archive — if this does not exist, foundational data work is prerequisite
  • LLM model selection and deployment (watsonx vs. third-party)
  • Legal/compliance review of AI-generated content for analyst-facing outputs
  • Integration with or adjacency to the Fact Review system referenced in multiple CAB wishlist items
KPI's
  • RFI draft turnaround time (target: 50% reduction)
  • % of RFI responses generated without manual rewrite
  • Analyst satisfaction score on response accuracy

Automated Fact Review & Consistency Check for Executive Outputs
Social Media & Influence
An agentic cross-check system that validates speeches, press quotes, and social posts against approved messaging, CEO Repository history, RFI Fact Review records, permissions datab
#2
Brief Description

Validates speeches, press quotes, and social posts against approved messaging, CEO Repository history, permissions databases, and style rules before release—ensuring consistency, accuracy, and brand compliance across all executive communications.

Process Owners
  • speechwriters
  • social media coordinators for executive accounts
  • legal/compliance reviewers
Future State: What AI Does
AI-Enabled Workflow
  • Executive communication (speech, press quote, or social post) is submitted for pre-release review
  • Agent cross-references all claims, statistics, and positioning statements against CEO Repository, approved messaging, and RFI Fact Review history
  • Agent checks tone, terminology, and formatting against SCG (Social Computing Guidelines) and brand style rules
  • Agent flags inconsistencies, unapproved claims, outdated statistics, or style violations with specific source citations
  • Human reviewer evaluates flagged items and approves or requests revision
  • Approved content is cleared for release; review log is archived for audit trail
AI Capabilities
  • ☑ Insight generation: Identify patterns of recurring inconsistencies across executive communications to proactively address root causes
  • ☑ Risk scoring / pre-review: Score each claim for accuracy risk based on source freshness, prior approval status, and deviation from approved messaging
  • ☑ Anomaly detection: Detect novel claims or statistics that have never appeared in approved sources, flagging for mandatory human review
  • ☑ Orchestration / routing: Route flagged items to appropriate reviewers based on content type (legal for claims, brand for style, SME for technical accuracy)
  • ☑ Executive summarization: Generate concise review reports highlighting all flagged items with specific source citations and confidence levels
  • ☑ Workflow automation: Automate first-pass review to reduce manual review burden and catch issues before human reviewers engage
Hypothesis
  • A Fact Review Agent would serve as an automated first-pass quality gate for all executive communications, cross-referencing claims against the institutional memory stored in CEO Repository and RFI databases. This reduces the risk of factual errors reaching external audiences while freeing human revi
Business Impact High

Reputational risk from inconsistent executive messaging is always present. [GAP] Have there been recent incidents of factual errors reaching external audiences? What is the current review cycle time?

Future Extensions & Reusability
  • Fact-checking engine directly reusable for Crisis Content Fact-Review & Clearance Workflow (Workflow 9)
  • SCG/style validation applicable to all content production across MCC — social posts, paid media copy, thought leadership
  • Claim extraction patterns reusable for RFI Response Agent (Workflow 1) quality validation
  • Architecture extensible to validate communications in non-English markets with geo-specific style rules
Feasibility Low
  • CEO Repository must be accessible via API for real-time cross-referencing
  • SCG rules must be encoded in machine-readable format (not just PDF documents)
  • Legal/compliance sign-off on AI-assisted review for executive-facing content
New Tech Required
  • LLM with claim extraction and semantic matching capabilities
  • Structured API access to CEO Repository and RFI Fact Review database
  • SCG/style guide encoded as machine-readable rules
  • Audit trail and logging for compliance
Primary Friction Points
  • 1. Manual / repetitive processes: Manual cross-referencing of claims against multiple source systems is time-intensive and error-prone
  • 2. Content / data scattered across systems: Approved messaging, fact-check history, and style rules exist in separate systems with no unified validation layer
  • 3. Handoff / coordination delays: Multiple reviewers (legal, brand, SME) must each independently validate different aspects of the same content
  • 4. Compliance / governance overhead: SCG compliance and brand style adherence require domain-specific knowledge that varies across content types
  • 5. Approval bottlenecks: Multi-stage approval process slows time-to-publish for time-sensitive executive communications
Technical Requirements
Engagement Needed
  • CIO partnership for LLM and NLP integration
  • Executive communications team for workflow integration and testing
Additional Discovery
  • Current review process: who reviews, how long, how many steps?
  • Frequency and volume of executive communications requiring review
  • Existing CEO Repository structure and API availability
Dependencies & Constraints
  • CEO Repository must be accessible via API for real-time cross-referencing
  • SCG rules must be encoded in machine-readable format (not just PDF documents)
  • Legal/compliance sign-off on AI-assisted review for executive-facing content
  • Adjacent to RFI Response Agent — shared fact-checking infrastructure
KPI's
  • % of factual errors caught before publication (target: >95%)
  • Time to complete first-pass review (target: <10 min per doc)
  • Reduction in manual review cycles per executive output

Executive Briefing Doc Creator/Assistant – Gen 2
Social Media & Influence
A multi-source synthesis agent that generates executive briefing documents by combining CEO Repository, IBV research, and approved external sources — producing dynamic Q&A briefs,
#5
Brief Description

Generates executive briefing documents by combining CEO Repository, IBV research, and approved external sources into dynamic Q&A briefs, issue/risk heat-maps, and per-audience variants with auto-citations and “what's changed since last briefing” summaries.

Process Owners
  • speechwriters
  • EA staff
  • executive leadership
Future State: What AI Does
AI-Enabled Workflow
  • Briefing request is initiated with target audience, topic, and event context parameters
  • Agent queries CEO Repository, IBV research, approved external sources, and prior briefing history
  • Agent generates structured briefing document with executive summary, Q&A section, issue/risk heat-map, and key talking points
  • Agent produces per-audience variants tailored to the specific meeting context (customer, analyst, government, etc.)
  • Agent generates 'what's changed since last briefing' differential highlighting new information
  • Human reviewer validates, edits, and approves the briefing for delivery
  • Feedback from the executive engagement is captured to improve future briefing quality
AI Capabilities
  • ☑ Insight generation: Identify relevant issues, risks, and opportunities specific to the briefing audience by analyzing cross-domain signals
  • ☑ Drafting / content generation: Generate structured briefing documents with executive summary, Q&A, risk heat-map, and talking points
  • ☑ Risk scoring / pre-review: Issue/risk heat-map generation scoring emerging topics by relevance and potential impact
  • ☑ Anomaly detection: 'What's changed since last briefing' detection — identifying new information that wasn't in prior versions
  • ☑ Orchestration / routing: Route briefing drafts through appropriate review chains based on audience and sensitivity level

Advocacy Agent
Social Media & Influence
An AI agent that enables executives and employees to instantly generate personalized LinkedIn posts from real-time headlines and bylines surfaced from IBM's priority media list in
#6
Brief Description

Enables executives and employees to instantly generate personalized LinkedIn posts from real-time headlines and social kits surfaced from IBM's priority media list in Meltwater, aligned to key planned and unplanned moments.

Process Owners
  • Jonathan Zeller (Social Media & Influence Lead)
  • Naja McDonald (Social League/Advocacy Programs)
  • Lucy Linthwaite (Meltwater owner
  • Comms team)
  • IBM executives and advocates
  • Comms team members
User Groups
  • Jonathan Zeller (Social Media & Influence Lead), Naja McDonald (Social League/Advocacy Programs), Lucy Linthwaite (Meltwater owner, Comms team), IBM executives and advocates, Comms team members
Future State: What AI Does
AI-Enabled Workflow
  • Meltwater surfaces real-time headline/byline from IBM's priority media list or advocacy page publishes social kit for a key moment
  • Agent ingests the media content, extracts key messages, and cross-references against IBM's approved positioning and narrative
  • Agent generates personalized post copy suggestions for each executive/advocate, adapted to their individual tone of voice and audience
  • Suggested posts are pushed to executives/advocates via integrated channel (Meltwater, email, or direct notification)
  • Executive/advocate reviews, personalizes, and publishes on their LinkedIn profile
  • Agent captures engagement metrics from published posts and feeds back into content optimization
  • Over time, agent learns individual tone of voice patterns to produce increasingly personalized suggestions
AI Capabilities
  • ☑ Insight generation: Identify which media moments and bylines are most relevant to each executive's domain and audience, prioritizing high-impact opportunities
  • ☑ Drafting / content generation: Generate personalized LinkedIn post copy adapted to each executive's tone of voice, audience, and domain expertise — per Jonathan: 'based on how the AI learns it gets smarter, it could understand somebody's tone of voice over time'
  • ☑ Risk scoring / pre-review: Screen generated post copy against approved messaging and SCG guidelines before delivery to executives
  • ☑ Anomaly detection: Detect unexpected media moments — like the Anthropic/Claude Code news — that create urgent advocacy opportunities
  • ☑ Orchestration / routing: Route media signals to the right executives based on topic relevance, seniority, and audience alignment
  • ☑ Executive summarization: Synthesize media bylines into concise, action-oriented post copy that captures key messages

  • Composed workflow is tested and deployed for the specific use case
  • Post-use, feedback is captured and workflow patterns are archived for future reuse

  • ☑ Orchestration / routing: Core capability — the orchestration layer is the primary AI function, coordinating data flow, sequencing, and human-in-the-loop checkpoints across composed agent workflows

  • Architecture patterns applicable to MCC-wide agent orchestration beyond Corporate Affairs

  • Component standardization requires coordination across CA functions

Crisis Signal Triage and Response Agent
Social Media & Influence
A high-priority agent that continuously monitors brand signal feeds across Meltwater and other monitoring platforms, applies sentiment and urgency scoring to incoming alerts, and r
#12
Brief Description

Continuously monitors brand signal feeds across monitoring platforms, applies sentiment and urgency scoring to incoming alerts, and routes only actionable signals to appropriate teams with recommended response actions.

Process Owners
  • Jonathan Zeller (SMNI Lead)
  • Comms team (Meltwater users)
  • Lucy Linthwaite (Meltwater owner)
  • Social League team (Naja McDonald)
  • Brand channel managers
User Groups
  • Jonathan Zeller (SMNI Lead), Comms team (Meltwater users), Lucy Linthwaite (Meltwater owner), Social League team (Naja McDonald), Brand channel managers
Future State: What AI Does
AI-Enabled Workflow
  • Agent continuously ingests brand signal feeds from Meltwater, Sprinklr, and other monitoring platforms
  • Agent applies NLP-based sentiment analysis and urgency scoring to each incoming signal
  • Agent classifies signals: actionable (route to team), informational (archive and trend), noise (filter out)
  • Actionable signals are routed to the appropriate team member with context summary and recommended response/course of action
  • Team member reviews the recommendation, decides on action, and executes response
  • Agent captures response decisions and outcomes to improve scoring accuracy over time
  • Agent generates daily/weekly trend summaries of signal patterns for strategic planning
AI Capabilities
  • ☑ Insight generation: Surface signal patterns and emerging trends across monitoring feeds that human reviewers would miss when processing individual alerts
  • ☑ Drafting / content generation: Generate recommended response actions for each actionable signal, giving team members a starting point rather than a blank slate
  • ☑ Risk scoring / pre-review: Urgency scoring on every incoming signal — high/medium/low with specific risk factors identified
  • ☑ Anomaly detection: Detect unusual signal patterns (volume spikes, new source clusters, unexpected sentiment shifts) that may indicate emerging crisis or opportunity
  • ☑ Orchestration / routing: Route actionable signals to the right team members based on topic, severity, and expertise alignment
  • ☑ Executive summarization: Synthesize multiple related signals into consolidated context summaries, reducing information overload for human reviewers
Hypothesis
  • The Crisis Signal Triage Agent directly addresses the most acute operational pain point identified by the Social Media & Influence team: the constant burden of manually evaluating incoming brand signals. In a high-frequency monitoring environment, the team processes significant noise to identify gen
Business Impact Medium

The team identified this as their 'most acute operational pain point.' Every hour spent on false-positive evaluation is an hour not spent on strategic response or proactive reputation building.   • Triage framework applicable to any IBM domain dealing with high-volume monitoring (security, customer feedback, competitive intelligence)
  • Escalation patterns feed into Crisis Content Fact-Review (Workflow 9) and NOVA Extension (Workflow 8)

  • 2. Content / data scattered across systems: Signals come from multiple platforms (Meltwater, Sprinklr) with no unified triage layer
  • 3. Handoff / coordination delays: Signal triage to response action involves informal handoffs — person who identifies the signal may not be the person who should respond

Brief Description

Transforms the Social and Influence Airtable Editorial Calendar from a passive tracking tool into an active orchestration layer that ingests content submissions, applies scheduling logic, flags gaps and conflicts, and generates draft content briefs for open slots.

  • Approved content flows to distribution channels via unified pipeline

  • ☑ Orchestration / routing: Core capability — orchestrate the full content lifecycle from submission through scheduling, approval, and distribution as a unified pipeline
  • ☑ Executive summarization: Generate calendar status summaries for editorial meetings and stakeholder updates

Channel Governance and Access Management Agent
Social Media & Influence
An agent that automates the Social Media Channel Access and Governance workflow — monitoring HR and organizational roster feeds, routing requests through a defined approval chain,
#16
Brief Description

Automates the Social Media Channel Access and Governance workflow by monitoring HR/organizational roster feeds, routing requests through approval chains, documenting access grants/revocations in an audit trail, and flagging compliance anomalies.

Process Owners
  • Ellen Cornillon (Governance & Compliance
User Groups
  • Ellen Cornillon (Governance & Compliance: one-person team), Jonathan Zeller (SMNI Lead), managers of social media account users (~60 people connected to LinkedIn account alone), 1Password administrators
Future State: What AI Does
AI-Enabled Workflow
  • Agent monitors HR and organizational roster feeds for employee joins, departures, and role changes
  • For departures: agent automatically flags accounts requiring access revocation and routes to Ellen for execution, with priority flagging for departed employees retaining access
  • For new access requests: manager submits request, agent routes through defined approval chain, documents approval, and triggers access provisioning
  • Agent documents every access change with timestamps, approvals, and screenshots (replacing current manual Word document process)
  • For continuing business need checks: agent automatically generates review lists by account, identifies users whose access hasn't been revalidated within the defined cycle, and sends manager verification requests
  • Agent maintains a real-time access inventory across all platforms — always current, queryable, and audit-ready
  • Agent flags compliance anomalies: expired validations, departed users with active access, unauthorized changes
AI Capabilities
  • ☑ Insight generation: Analyze access patterns to identify compliance risks — users with access to accounts outside their current role, departed employees with lingering access, unusual access request patterns
  • ☑ Risk scoring / pre-review: Compliance risk scoring — prioritize access reviews based on role sensitivity, account exposure (brand-level vs. regional), and time since last validation
  • ☑ Anomaly detection: Flag compliance anomalies in real time: departed employees retaining access, access grants without approval documentation, access to accounts inconsistent with current role
  • ☑ Orchestration / routing: Orchestrate the full access lifecycle — request → approval → provisioning → documentation → revalidation → revocation — as a governed, automated workflow
  • ☑ Executive summarization: Generate audit-ready access reports, continuing business need check summaries, and compliance status dashboards
  • ☑ Workflow automation: Automate the manual tracking, documentation, and revalidation process that Ellen currently manages alone across multiple platforms and systems
Hypothesis
  • The Channel Governance Agent directly addresses what the SMNI team identified as a 'strong early automation candidate because the workflow is well-defined and the pain is ongoing.' Ellen is a one-person team managing access governance across LinkedIn, Twitter, Instagram, Sprinklr, and 1Password for

High for compliance risk mitigation.
